    <li> This may be the first truly &amp;#34;fogless&amp;#34; mirror I&#x27;ve had!  It&#x27;s a bit of a nuisance to fill it with hot water each time, and the squeegee is not terribly effective, but overall it permits me to shave comfortably in the shower.  The razor rest on the bottom is quite handy.</li>
    <li> Not worth $40. More like about $20. Light is pretty useless. Fog-less part works.</li>
    <li> Amazing product. Perfect solution. Love the LED  lights and no fog. Crystal clear and easy to install.</li>
    <li> So far so good.  The mirror comes with silicone to glue to the wall but I drilled a couple of small holes in the mounting bracket and used some drywall mollys to mount in my tiled shower stall.  Works great.  Has not fogged yet and is a very clear image.</li>
    <li> ***UPDATED REVIEW 12/8/14***  After receiving a faulty unit initially (see old review below) I reordered and checked the new one over, not finding the flaw I did with the first.  Mounting was easy and simple enough with the pre-attached adhesive strips and tube of silicone.  I cleaned the side of the wall where this would go and mounted according to the instructions, waiting 24 hours before attaching the mirror itself.      This is the second shower mirror I&#x27;ve ever had and I&#x27;m an avid Headblader, so I&#x27;m using a razor on my face or head nearly every time I&#x27;m in the shower.  The first mirror was round  (~5 in diamter) with a covered LED strip around the edges (dim) and a hanger for the razor below (flimsy, doesn&#x27;t fit all razors); it was mounted using suction cups (which would fail, loudly) and had some kind of anti-fogging chemical applied (which worked for about a month but prevented cleaning afterwards).  I won&#x27;t waste any more time on the deficiencies of that unit, but wanted to include that as narrative for this review.    While only installed for a couple of weeks now, it feels solidly mounted to the wall.  The mirror is nice and large and offers some magnification.  The LED is bright enough to shave from when the bathroom lights are dimmed low, something that can happen on early mornings for me.  Filling the reservoir is a MUST to prevent fogging - it&#x27;s how it works - and I&#x27;ve had no issues with fogging at all.  The attached squeegee can remove water drops easily to keep the surface clear.    Just a couple of minor gripes, though.  While the LED is bright, you really are only using reflected light on your face.  This necessitates me having to lean in very close to the mirror for the LED to light my face or head (not an issue when the lights in the bathroom are on full).  Putting the reservoir back in place can be a bit tricky unless you press your face against the side of the shower wall - it would be nice if it were a little easier (maybe experience or more than 2 weeks will do it?).  Finally, the platform beneath the mirror (the box shows a razor laying on it) is much closer to the bottom of the mirror than that picture indicates.  A bit more room would make it easier getting hands on/off the razor.    In all I&#x27;m very pleased with this mirror compared to my previous one.        ***OLD REVIEW***  Upon receiving (which was as timely as ever) I unboxed and looked everything over to make sure there were no glaring issues.  I noticed the battery cover seemed to have been assembled incorrectly or improperly labeled.  The screw tops were plastic and large enough for fingers and were keyed with a triangle, designed to be a guide to lock or unlock the battery compartment with a simple quarter of a turn.  I noted that one of the screwtops was oriented correctly, pointing at the lock that was closed; the other was 180 degrees off.  I turned the mislabeled one first in the direction that it should go to unlock and it did - other side worked as well.  I placed the batteries and put the cover back on and tightened one screw down, but the misaligned one from earlier didn&#x27;t budge - I had placed it in the \\&quot;correct\\&quot; position per the diagram, opposite what it had been.  I switched it back to where it was oriented and attempted to tighten it down and the screwtop snapped freely from the metal screw it was attached to.    I returned to Amazon, but was a bit dismayed that I could only return and get a refund, not do an exchange.</li>
    <li> I was so excited to give this to my husband for his birthday.  When I finally had time to mount it to the smooth glass shower enclosure wall, I took extra care to follow the directions for prepping the surface with an alcohol prep pad and keeping the shower dry over a weekend to ensure it would stay securely attached. We have hard, ceramic tile floors and if the mount failed, I was certain the mirror would be toast.  My hub loved the mirror. It&#x27;s nice and bright and the pivot made it easy for me to see into it as well, and I&#x27;m a foot shorter than my husband--okay, on my tiptoes. Six or seven months later, I found the mirror on the floor, broken, with all the silicone still on the glass enclosure. So, although liked the mirror very much and it definitely stayed fog free I&#x27;m disappointed that it didn&#x27;t stay securely fasten to the wall. The mirror and lighting, however, really great! Unfortunately, we&#x27;re back to a small, suction cup attached mirror.</li>
    <li> The mirror pops off the mount WAY too easily.  I bought it for my husband for Father&#x27;s Day, he seems to like it, but every time he goes to squeegee it off after his shower, it pops off the mount and totally irritates him.  It&#x27;s a shame, because it&#x27;s an otherwise great product.  If you can live with it jumping off the wall, go for it.  It&#x27;s good size, lights up well, does the trick, but that&#x27;s a major flaw that the manufacturers need to adress in future design.</li>

    <li> My wife and I have purchased numerous \\&quot;fogless\\&quot; mirrors in the past, paying anywhere from $15-$40, only to realize the  \\&quot;foglessness\\&quot; is only temporary in nature... and almost never longer than 3 months.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While we&#x27;ve only had this one for a bit over a month, it appears to be the real deal. The light with two intensity settings is a really nice touch.  The squeegee is another neat feature but, it could be better sized to matched the mirror (minor gripe).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So far, well worth the few extra bucks over its competitors. One additional minor gripe is that after the cavity on the unit is filled with water and rehung onto the base, the mirror has enough weight that it sometimes wants to tip downward... but it is easily readjustable to the preferred position, and holds firm as long as you don&#x27;t touch it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After 4 months with other mirrors, I would be cussing them each and every morning as I squirm about the shower trying to find that one spot on the mirror that I can see enough of my face to properly shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update:  11/02/12 - The bracket no longer holds the weight of the mirror when filled with water, as the tilt mechanism has given out. They have apparently changed the design or construction in some way to make the mechanism more durable.  I received the replacement tilt mechanism, and installed in about 1 minute... quick and easy! My mirror is like new again!  Thanks to the ToiletTree Products team for taking care of the customer.     <li> I love shaving in the shower where I can wash my face in hot soapy water, then applying lather and, with the mirror very close, very clear, and with the lights on shave with my Gillette Power Fusion razor which buzzes and vibrates while I shave. CONS: [1]The mirror is, frankly, dis-oriented by 90 degrees - it would be a whole lot more useful if the top to bottom dimension was the larger one - i.e., most people I know have faces that are longer than they are wide yet this mirror is oriented (and can&#x27;t be changed) with the larger dimension going side to side. [2]The re-mounting once filled with water is adequate but you&#x27;re doing it blindly since the mounting slot is on the back so it&#x27;s a bit awkward. Since my mirror is going to be useful again, I thought I&#x27;d change out the batteries since they were near death (LED lights were very  dim).  After my shower, I took the mirror over to my sink and, using a quarter, turned the two sealing screws to their respective \\&quot;unlock\\&quot; pictures. The top of the battery compartment opened just fine but the bottom, despite the sealing screw indicating it was unlocked, would not budge. I peaked inside of the top to see how the locking mechanism worked and was very confident all was in order and it was likely just a little stuck due to not having been opened for awhile.  Sliding the screw along the seam between the door and battery compartment, I applied a little pressure to get it unstuck.  To my surprise, the door finally popped open but when I turned the door over, I could see that the locking mechanism was still locked to the plastic piece it recessed into...and that piece had broken away from inside the battery compartment housing! :(  Upon further investigation, I could see that the plastic piece that was supposed to turn to lock the door, was indeed stuck and the metal screw that attached it to the outside sealing screw just spun when the sealing screw turned -- I was never getting that door off.  Even after tightening the metal screw, I couldn&#x27;t get the two separated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So now, I had a part on the way to make my mirror useful again, but a broken battery door that rendered the LED system useless due to now being unsealable. How&#x27;s that for irony? :)  This morning, I was actually very confident that ToiletTree customer service would make things right, just from the painless interaction I had with them concerning the pivoting bracket a few days ago....and I wasn&#x27;t disappointed. After explaining my situation to the gal on the phone (including the part that is on its way), she asked if replacing the battery compartment door would fix the issue.  I indicated that, unfortunately, it would not, since the piece the bottom locking mechanism was supposed to lock to came detached from the inside battery compartment housing. I offered to send her a few pictures since (as you can see from above), it&#x27;s not the easiest thing to convey over the phone. She said, \\&quot;Oh no, no, that won&#x27;t be necessary.  What we&#x27;ll do is send you out a new mirror. I&#x27;ll expedite the shipment so you get it as soon as possible.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now THAT&#x27;s what I call customer service and a company that stands behind their product.  I have no doubt in my mind that if the screw failure is not an isolated incident, that, just like with the pivot bracket, ToiletTree will make things right.  Despite having the two issues I have, I have no reservations about recommending this product as well as the company.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2012-11-26: The replacement arrived.  I opened the box and all had arrived as promised.  *sigh* But I&#x27;m experiencing the exact same issue as before.  Turning the bottom screw to unlock does indeed unlock that lock on the battery compartment door but turning the top screw (felt rather tight) to unlock does not unlock the bottom screw lock. Having been through this once and eventually getting the door off, I know that any pressure I use to successfully dislodge the door will result in another broken unit. *sigh*  One more call to customer service tomorrow.  Such a great idea.  I haven&#x27;t seen any other complaints when searching \\&quot;screw\\&quot; through the reviews and if it weren&#x27;t such an easy action to take (i.e. turn screw to unlock symbol), I&#x27;d think there was something I was doing wrong.  Will update after customer service call.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2012-11-27: Talked to Kelly at customer service. She indicated that the screw issue was not normal let alone getting another unit and having it occur right out of the box. To ToiltTree&#x27;s credit, she&#x27;s sending another unit out and test the door herself before sending. She is also sending prepaid postage to have me send the other two units back so they can take a look.  Here&#x27;s hoping that this is just a freak occurrence. With an idiot-proof design of \\&quot;turn the arrow to the unlock symbol\\&quot;, I&#x27;m hoping that this is the case.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I continue to be impressed with how ToiletTree customer service handles themselves, how the company backs their product, and how they value a customer&#x27;s time and inconvenience. Furthermore, in looking at the tilt mechanism myself right now, I can see why he was so concerned. It truly is a flimsy design. I wonder if I didn&#x27;t peel the cover of BOTH sides of the tape, which resulted in the bracket not sticking to the wall while the adhesive dried. If so, that&#x27;s quite embarrassing and not the fault of the company.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also mentioned below that the pivoting mechanism seemed rather flimsy, and I&#x27;m happy to say that this replacement they sent me seems much sturdier.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Anyways, now that the mirror is in place, I enjoy it quite a bit.  I went over what I like about it in the older review below the dotted line, but I&#x27;ll rattle them off again in a list here:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) Nice and large viewing area.&lt;br /&gt;2) Stays completely fog-free as advertised.  And this is the most important feature.&lt;br /&gt;3) It has a shelf for my razor.&lt;br /&gt;4) It has LED lights that do an adequate job of lighting up my face.&lt;br /&gt;5) It has a squeegee for cleaning water droplets off the mirror. Very handy to have.&lt;br /&gt;6) It&#x27;s sticking to the wall VERY securely. This thing is not falling anytime soon, if ever.&lt;br /&gt;7) Toilettree Products really does a good job listening to their customers, and are VERY quick about fixing any issues.  A+ customer support!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, let me list off some things that could be improved:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) While the shelf is nice, it should be bigger.  It&#x27;s kinda small, at least for my Gillette ProGlide 3-in-1 Styler monstrosity thing. It should have some kind of lip around the edge to minimize the risk of your razor falling off. Also a holder for a can of shaving cream would be nice.&lt;br /&gt;2) Plastics feel too cheap for the price tag. This thing is pricey, and I feel that the materials it&#x27;s made out of should reflect that. Maybe it should have a nice rubberized shelf so your razor won&#x27;t slide around on it or soft touch surfaces around the edges for when you pick the mirror up to fill it with water.  Some metal pieces incorporated into the design would be nice as well.  It just needs something that shows/feels premium since this item carries a premium price tag.&lt;br /&gt;3) The difference between the brightness settings for the LED lights is minimal.  Like I said below, I had a hard time telling the difference.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So as you can see, the positives far outweigh the negatives.  This is a very smart idea that works, and has a company behind it that actually has quality customer support. Now I just have to see how this holds up over time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I highly recommend this mirror to anyone. As this company strives to improve their product, I can&#x27;t wait to see what they will do next.  Good job guys and gals!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-ORIGINAL REVIEW-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I originally bought the cheaper non-lit version of this mirror a while back. It said that it was impossible for this mirror to fog up; and the claim was completely accurate. When filled with water, the mirror stayed clear for the entire duration of my shower. And the mirror was a generous size which is always nice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, after about 3-4 months, I noticed that the mirrored surface was starting to erode away at the corners from the inside, and everytime I dumped the water out, little black flecks of stuff would fall out and go down the drain. I admit that I would leave the water in the mirror instead of dumping it out right away, so maybe that had something to do with the erosion, but still that is not an excuse for the degradation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So then I noticed that there was a \\&quot;deluxe\\&quot; LED-lit model of the mirror, and I bought it about 2-3 weeks ago thinking I would make sure to dump the water out right away to perhaps prevent the mirrored surface from eroding away again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I received the mirror, and was surprised to see it was even bigger than the first mirror, which was really nice. Then I tried to use the included adhesive to stick the mirror to the shower wall, and it wouldn&#x27;t stick. It kept sliding down no matter how long I held it on the wall for. I never had this issue with the first mirror.  So I eventually gave up and used super glue to stick it to the wall.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then the first time I filled the reservoir with water, it started leaking from FOUR(!) separate spots on the bottom. All the water would leak out within 1 minute.  Also, the product was supposed to have two brightness settings for the LED lights, but this one only had one setting. It would only turn them on and then off again.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I emailed the company and promptly received a replacement mirror. I filled it with water and it did not leak.  It also had the two brightness setting as described, although the difference between the brightness setting was so minimal I spent a good five minutes trying to determine if there was really any difference at all between them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shelf on this model was the same size as the first mirror I had, but because the mirror itself was bigger, it was harder to reach the shelf to put my razor on. But this wasn&#x27;t a big issue to me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The pivoting mechanism on this model also seemed VERY flimsy, unlike the first mirror I had. I filled the mirror with water and used the included squeegee (nice touch) to clean the water droplets off the mirrored surface. In doing so, the mirror pivoted down from the position I wanted it in so I had to readjust the mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now this morning, the mirror fell off the wall (remember I used super glue because the included adhesive wouldn&#x27;t work for me)and broke my razor. The pivoting mechanism completely separated from the mirror, although I may be able to put it back together.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m pretty ticked about the issues I&#x27;ve had with this mirror, partly due to the price of it.  This is a LOT of money for a shower mirror.  The concept is genius, but the build quality is not representative of the price tag.  You are paying for the idea of it; not the quality.     <li> I ordered this mirror for my husband who shaves in the shower (heavy beard).  Anyway, it went together quickly, and works perfectly.  I asked him to rate it, and he said &amp;#34;Give it five stars!&amp;#34;.  It doesn&#x27;t fog up like the one it replaced because you fill the back of it with water.  When I asked my husband if he thought that the filling and emptying was a nuisance, he said, &amp;#34;not in the least.&amp;#34;  As for the lighting, it also is perfect.  His old mirror lit from the bottom and would shut off after an allotted amount of time.  This mirror lights completely around its perimeter giving the user better lighting, and the switch is manual.  The user just shuts it off when finished.  So, all that said, my husband recommends this mirror for anyone who needs a mirror in the shower.  NOTE: One reviewer remarked on the width vs. height, stating that the mirror should be taller rather than wider.  My husband finds the dimensions perfect.  After thinking on it myself, I can see that the height issue might be important for a man who shaves his head.  Still, the mirror tilts and should accommodate that issue as well.  In any case, I don&#x27;t believe anyone who orders this mirror will be disappointed.</li>

    <li> I have purchased many &amp;#34;fogless&amp;#34; mirrors in the past...none of them work. Don&#x27;t get me wrong, they are good for a month or so, but then...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This one, because you fill it with warm water, actually solves the problem. Fog occurs because of the temperature difference. Without getting into a physics lesson, condensate (fog) forms on a cooler surface because, as the water in the air cools, it forms droplets, thus clouding your mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This mirror is designed that you fill with warm/hot water when getting in the shower. Because the mirror is warmed by the water, it stays of even enought temperature with the shower, that no condensate (fog) occurs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Great design and flawless execution. This will be my last shaving mirror.</li>

    <li> Day 1: I received this item in the mail a few hours ago. Out of the box I noticed a scratch on the frame of the mirror but decided it will be forgotten in time. I followed the directions, cleaned the wall surface with soap and water, then with alcohol and waited for the surface to dry. When I tried to apply the silicon glue to the frame I realized the contents of the tube were dried up, nothing was coming out and it was completely useless. Fortunately I had some Gorilla glue and used that in combination with the sticky back tape that came in the box to attach the frame to the tiled wall. I immediately realized the plastic frame is not straight. Trying to push it down to the tile was a complete waste of time and eventually I had to settle for holding it down with some masking tape. I will remove the tape to see how well it is attached tomorrow and will share the rest of my findings then. So far, I will give it a generous 1 out of 5.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Day 2: My substitute gorilla glue has dried and I attached the mirror. After an hour run on the treadmill it was time to take a shower and give the new mirror a try. I followed the instructions, removed the mirror and filled the reservoir in the back with warm water from the shower and true to their word the mirror did not fog up once during my long hot shower! I shaved with the LED lights on and it was nice to actually see me face clearly for a change :) I had been using the same old Z&#x27;fogless mirror for a few years and it was pretty scratched up from falling and a bit tarnished from constant humidity. So, I upgrade my rating from 1 to 3 stars and will hold my final judgement until more use. I should also note that I received a very timely response to my initial post from the President of the company owning up to the problems and willing to do whatever is necessary to make things right with me. I have to admit that kind of customer service is very nice and representative of a caring company. I have a few thoughts/suggestions to make this a better product. Some of these may prove to be unnecessary after further use but here they are anyways:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Better quality of glue or perhaps two tubes from different batches/suppliers in case one is dried up :)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Better quality control to make sure there are no scratches on the mirror or its frame. This may be very difficult to do as I am sure they are manufactured in China and are handled by people during assembly and packing so it is impossible to avoid a few small scratches every once in a while. Having said that, for this amount of money at retail I think a perfect product is more fitting and expected. Those with tiny scratches and other small imperfections can be sold through liquidators and in other markets at lesser prices.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. I am a bit concerned about the wear and tear of the plastic tilting mechanism over time. Using metal parts would have been worse given rusting problems but perhaps making that portion removable and replaceable would be a good idea for the next generation. Also, it is hard to remove the mirror without causing some tilting as it is sort of flimsy. Perhaps this is an area where some improvement can be made in the next version.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. I realize filling the reservoir with hot water is the key to keeping the mirror from fogging up but perhaps there is a better way to empty and refill the reservoir without having to remove it and having to deal with all the tilting issues and any chances of dropping and scratching the mirror. A tube with a valve at the bottom of the mirror can be used to drain the reservoir and another with a large funnel like top can be used to refill it. I realize this is a rather rudimentary approach but I am sure the designers of the product can think of more innovative approaches to tackle this challenge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. Having batteries in any device near the shower and water and keeping them from rusting is rather challenging. We will see how well these are sealed overtime.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In conclusion, after one use, the mirror works as advertised and the lighting is a nice useful feature. I will update my findings over time so stay tuned. Of course my wife still has to use it and she may have a thing or two to add :)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Week 2: The Gorilla glue I used to attach the mirror base to the wall has held up fine and when filled with warm water the mirror does not fog but that is all the positives I can say about it while giving myself credit for using a better grade of glue since I had no choice. Unfortunately, already the mirror can not hold the weight of the water it needs in order of it to work as advertised. This is due to the cheap plastic mechanism used to set the angle of the mirror which I do not change but gets moved everyday when I have to remove the old water and add fresh warm water. Further, the adding and emptying of water has become a time consuming pain which requires one to also wipe the water drops from the surface of the mirror. The supplied blade is also not perfect in removing the water from the surface and leaves many trails on the mirror. A better design would have used batteries and an electrical filament to heat the back of the mirror quickly even if it would have required more or separate batteries. In all, I find this mirror to be of very poor quality and am going to send it back. I only hope to be able to remove the base from the wall without breaking it or leaving a mark on the tiles. Water droplets may gather on the surface of the mirror, but if you periodically \\&quot;pre-treat\\&quot; the mirror with actual windshield washer fluid, you&#x27;ll find that the water beads up and runs off a lot better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The LED light is white and bright - the lower setting is just fine, though of course depending on your bathroom lighting you may want to use the brighter setting (particularly at night).     <li> This review will be categorical, detailing specific points of interest for this product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-In the Box-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The contents of the box included everything that was needed to both mount and operate this device: mounting bracket, mirror unit, 3xAA batteries, squeegee, and silicone adhesive.  The instructions for mounting and operation are what we have all undoubtedly come to expect, which is brief; however, the instructions were detailed and consise enough to leave no one confused about how to either instal or use this device.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-Installation-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The installation instructions call for the use of the adhesive squares attached to the rear of the mounting bracket, as well as the application of the included adhesive silicone.  It is important to note here that I DID NOT follow these instructions when mounting this product.  Instead, I used Command waterproof mounting strips found below.  If you are in any way uncertain when installing this product, I do advise that you follow the included instructions to the letter, as I have likely voided the product warranty by doing what I did.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You are going to want to first prep the surface of the shower prior to using any method of installation where adhesive makes contact with the shower wall.  As I am sure we are all aware, repeated use of our showers results in this wonderful film that we must clean periodically.  Applying any adhesive to that film will cause the adhesive to bond to it, rather than the wall surface.  I used a healthy amount of Windex Commercial, because it contains ammonia.  Why?  Because a good portion of the cleaners we use on a daily basis leave a residue of thier own, which can and will interfere with adhesion.  I allowed the Windex to sit on the surface for approximately 2-3 minutes before using an abrasive pad to scrub the wall.  I then used a dry cloth to wipe away the moisture before using an alcohol prep pad on the surface I had just cleaned.  The instructions do call for the use of alcohol, and you may find this an unnecessary step, here&#x27;s why it isn&#x27;t:  when exposed to air, alcohol evaporates without leaving any sort of residue, which ensures that the adhesive can bond directly to the surface it is being applied to.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Once the surface was cleaned, I removed the adhesive squares from the back of the mounting bracket, replacing them with the Command mounting strips (see included picture for placement).  I allowed the shower wall and mounting strips approximately 2-3 minutes before applying the bracket to the shower wall.  I then applied pressure to the bracket, to seat the mounting strips, for appoximately 30 seconds.  At this point I applied pressure to the tray on the bracket to ensure a solid bond before hanging the mirror unit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You will notice that I again applied pressure to the tray on the bracket once the mirror unit was in place (see included picture), deflecting the tray quite a bit.  I did this to demonstrate the effectiveness of the above installation.  While I have no doubt this unit will stay where it is until the end of time (I have hung heavy LED units with command strips that are in place after over a year), there is absolutely nothing wrong with the recommended installation.  The adhesive squares in combination with the silicone will hold the unit in place so long as you properly prep the surface.  I have read a few reviews of people gripping about the unit not staying in place, and that is because they didn&#x27;t properly prepare the surface.  You can glue a Buick to the side of a building, so long as the surface is properly prepared (Of course, there are other considerations when one decides to glue a car to a building, but I think you get my point).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Command Strips: http://smile.amazon.com/gp/product/B000WSNM9Q/ref&#x3D;oh_aui_detailpage_o00_s00?ie&#x3D;UTF8&amp;psc&#x3D;1&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-In the Shower-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Filling the unit is pretty straightfoward and easy, with the top of the unit housing a fairly large opening to accomodate filling.  I used hot water as instructed, and was surprised that the only thing that wound up on the surface of the mirror were water dropplets from splashing.  I have used other units, even units that continiously cycle water behind the mirror, and all of them have devolped \\&quot;fog\\&quot;.  Using the mirror was pretty simple, though it is constructed in such a way as to magnify your face (or whatever you happen to want to aim the mirror at), so you do need to be standing fairly close to get an undistorted reflection.  The magnification made shaving my face easier than using a conventional wall mirror, primarily because I could literally see the pores in my face.  As I mentioned, water droplets did form on the surface of the mirror, and the included squeegee worked to clear them .  The squeegee is not long enough to clear the mirror in one pass, but I didn&#x27;t have to spend more than a few seconds using it to get a clear reflection.  All in all, I was pleased with the mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The Light-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The light on the mirror is simple to activate, and is bright enough to illuminate your face if you need it.  I have a light built in to my shower, so I found no benefit in having a lit mirror.  If you shower in a cave however, you will likely find it quite useful.  The button on the side of the unit used to activate the light is easy to access, and doesn&#x27;t provide so much resistance that you need to be concerned with displacing the mirror.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The Pivot-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The mounting bracket has a built in pivot you can used to adjust the angle of the mirror up and down, which I found to be quite useful.  Not only was I able to use the mirror to shave my face, but the angle of the mirror also allowed me to groom my chest as well.  I suppose it goes without saying, but you could potentially use this mirror to shave any body reqion you so desired, depending on the mounting location of the mirror.  I noticed a few reviews that mentioned the noise the pivot makes when using it, as well as the fear of catastrophic failure as a result.  The pivot has teeth and uses friction to hold the mirror at the desired angle, so that is the \\&quot;snapping\\&quot; sound heard when adjusting the angle.  I played with the pivot pretty vigorously, and the mirror didn&#x27;t snap free and become airborn, so I don&#x27;t think you have anything to worry about.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-The Tray-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The tray that is part of the mounting bracket is plastic, but fairly rigid.  I was able to apply a good bit of pressure to the tray without causing a great deal of deflection.  Given the space between the mirror unit and the tray, you will have no issue storing your razor as depicted.  The tray will accomodate any small item(s) not prone to rolling without concern of the tray deflecting and dropping it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-Conclussions-&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, this is an excellent product that does everything that it claims to do.  The mirror and the mounting braket are solidly made, and the anti-fog system works flawlessly in my experience.  The magnification and pivot make the mirror fairly versatile.  It is easy to instal, easy to fill, and easy to maintain; which makes this mirror worth the price-point.s surprised that the only thing that wound up on the surface of the mirror were water dropplets from splashing.  I have used other units, even units that continiously cycle water behind the mirror, and all of them have devolped \\&quot;fog\\&quot;.  Using the mirror was pretty simple, though it is constructed in such a way as to magnify your face (or whatever you happen to want to aim the mirror at), so you do need to be standing fairly close to get an undistorted reflection.  The magnification made shaving my face easier than using a conventional wall mirror, primarily because I could literally see the pores in my face.  As I mentioned, water droplets did form on the surface of the mirror, and the included squeegee worked to clear them .  The squeegee is not long enough to clear the mirror in one pass, but I didn&#x27;t have to spend more than a few seconds using it to get a clear reflection.  All in all, I was pleased with the mirror.    -The Light-    The light on the mirror is simple to activate, and is bright enough to illuminate your face if you need it.  I have a light built in to my shower, so I found no benefit in having a lit mirror.  If you shower in a cave however, you will likely find it quite useful.  The button on the side of the unit used to activate the light is easy to access, and doesn&#x27;t provide so much resistance that you need to be concerned with displacing the mirror.    -The Pivot-    The mounting bracket has a built in pivot you can used to adjust the angle of the mirror up and down, which I found to be quite useful.  Not only was I able to use the mirror to shave my face, but the angle of the mirror also allowed me to groom my chest as well.  I suppose it goes without saying, but you could potentially use this mirror to shave any body reqion you so desired, depending on the mounting location of the mirror.  I noticed a few reviews that mentioned the noise the pivot makes when using it, as well as the fear of catastrophic failure as a result.  The pivot has teeth and uses friction to hold the mirror at the desired angle, so that is the \\&quot;snapping\\&quot; sound heard when adjusting the angle.  I played with the pivot pretty vigorously, and the mirror didn&#x27;t snap free and become airborn, so I don&#x27;t think you have anything to worry about.    -The Tray-    The tray that is part of the mounting bracket is plastic, but fairly rigid.  I was able to apply a good bit of pressure to the tray without causing a great deal of deflection.  Given the space between the mirror unit and the tray, you will have no issue storing your razor as depicted.  The tray will accomodate any small item(s) not prone to rolling without concern of the tray deflecting and dropping it.    -Conclussions-    All in all, this is an excellent product that does everything that it claims to do.  The mirror and the mounting braket are solidly made, and the anti-fog system works flawlessly in my experience.  The magnification and pivot make the mirror fairly versatile.  It is easy to instal, easy to fill, and easy to maintain; which makes this mirror worth the price-point.</li>
    <li> I really liked this mirror when i first got it.  It was bright and the anti-fog system works great.  However, over the past few months that i&#x27;ve owned it the \\&quot;gears\\&quot; that hold the mirror in position have stripped and now the mirror won&#x27;t stay up.  In other workds, the mirror can be roated up and down so you can see yourself, but that is all stripped and the mirror just points at the floor.  It started to do that when there was water in the mirror (it it heavier when filled with water - duh), but now it doesn&#x27;t even stay up when it&#x27;s empty.  The other thing is that if you leave the light on even once, the batteries will be completely run down.  Some kind of timer switch would be a nice feature, because most of us shave first thing in the morning (sleepy) and leaving a faint light on in the shower seems like something we would all do at some point.     <li> I&#x27;ve used many different types of \\&quot;fogless\\&quot; shower mirrors.  All of these products involve trade-offs among the triangle of Cost-Convenience-Quality factors.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve used the active type, which uses plumbed water to keep the mirror fog-free (works well but is pricey, and prone to breakage).  I&#x27;ve use the treated-surface mirrors which work to varying degrees, but consistently fail withing a few months.  I&#x27;ve also tried the heat-and-shave type that can&#x27;t seem to last my entire shave.  Of the ones I&#x27;ve tried, so far, this mirror offers the best balance of Cost, Convenience and Quality - that is, it works well, it&#x27;s easy to use, and it doesn&#x27;t rely on any complicated technologies to accomplish it&#x27;s job, meaning it should last for a good long time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The ToiletTree Deluxe LED Fogless Shower Mirror offers ample mirror space and an exceptionally bright, but well distributed, light.  The fogless technology is simple (warm water behind the mirror) and relies only on the same shower water that is causing the fog in the first place.  The mirror includes a squeegee that works well.  Though a subtlety, consistent squeegee use will extend the life of the mirror&#x27;s surface.  Folks with harder water, even if softened, will have particulate in the water that can accumulate on the mirror surface and \\&quot;dim\\&quot; the reflection over time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only negative, if it can even be considered as such, is that you must manually fill and empty the reservoir behind the mirror.  Still, when balanced against all of the positives, I consider this \\&quot;negative\\&quot; to be, at most, a minor inconvenience which I would happily take over the Cost and Quality negatives I&#x27;ve found in other products.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--UPDATE 5/11/13-- I have come to appreciate this mirror even more over the last couple of months.  The mirror has remained bright and clear, and the mount has remained firm.  In fact this mirror has the best viewable reflection of any of the shower-shave mirrors I&#x27;ve used. The problem with that is when the case is filled with water (that&#x27;s how they keep it fogless) the \\&quot;mirror\\&quot; bends thus distorting the image. (2) the wall mount needs to be glued to the wall, This creates an issue if and when you want to remove or move the mirror&#x27;s location, so be certain you put it exactly where you want it the first time. (3) the hinge to attach the mirror to the wall mount is also plastic. Thin plastic. two tiny pegs that snap in place.  This creates several issues: Unless you have a showerhead on a hose, you will have to unsnap the mirror every time you attempt to use it because you have to fill the mirror&#x27;s case with hot water to create the fogless environment. This mount is also supposed to make it so you can tilt the mirror, adjusting the angle up/down for better viewing. Unfortunately, the plastic is so thin and the peg is so small, these will surely break after a few attempts to remove/attach, and the weight of the water filled mirror is barely supported by the thin plastic hinge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Fortunately, By purchasing though Amazon, I was able to return this substandard product for a full refund.[[ASIN:B005OSQGN8 Pivoting Deluxe LED Fogless Shower Mirror with Squeegee]]</li>

    <li> This mirror was easy to install in our shower and it has stayed put using a combination of suction cups and a silicone adhesive, which, it is claimed, will hold the unit in place forever, but can be removed if necessary down the road. In use, one fills the reservoir with hot water from the shower, which keeps it from fogging. The built-in squeegee does the job well enough to remove most of the droplets that might collect on the mirror. The LED lights have two settings, one brighter than the other, accessed by a button on the right side when facing the unit. The user&#x27;s razor can be easily stored on the shelf below the mirror. Mirror size is quite adequate and it can be tilted up or down for users of different heights. Well-designed and very useful, especially in a shower without its own lighting.</li>
